Over the weekend I experienced what everyone's worst nightmare is.. a broken tooth. I was unaware of a cavity that had caused a lot of decay that resulted in a break. I knew that finding a dentist to treat me would be a difficult task because I am a cash patient (insurance doesn't kick in until March 1st). I was hesitant to even go because I knew I wouldn't be able to afford a crown etc with cash upfront, but convinced myself to go to one at least to see what it would take to fix my tooth.

I called Surf Smiles on 2/10/20 at about noon.. and they were able to fit me in same day! I mention that I was a cash patient and they quoted me a reasonable 89$ for a visit and x-rays. As I showed up to my appointment, I quickly noticed the well put together office. It's a beautiful spot. I was greeted by Dr. Hoeg at the front desk promptly and was asked to wait to be called. Not more than 10 minuted later, I was called to the back by Dr. Mark Warner who stated I would be seeing Dr. Hoeg for my appointment, but he was in a meeting so he would be starting my visit. (I thought that was very courteous because most of the time you're kept waiting when something like that occurs)

Dr. Mark Warner was very friendly and was quick to get my x-rays going. Dr. Hoeg came in shortly after and I was amazed by how nice he is!! Seriously just a genuinely nice individual. While I was getting my tooth looked at, Dr. Madeline Warner came in to introduce herself (seriously how nice is that?). I quickly realized that this practice is family run and they care about their patients as individuals. You're not just a number or price tag to this family! Dr. Hoeg continued to examine me and was very conservative in my treatment as he was trying to avoid a root canal (which I very much appreciate!!) I expressed to him that I am a cash pay patient and would be interested in a temporary solution to my tooth problem if need be until my insurance kicked in. I was blown away with his work ethic and compassion as he completely restored my tooth and was able to work with me on pricing. You literally can't even tell I had half of my tooth missing. (pictures listed as reference)

Not only am I (and my whole family) a patient for life, but I am actually excited to return and work on my other dental issues. I will continue to rave about this practice as long as they are in business! Thank you Surf Smiles, you have restored my smile (and faith in humanity).<//Review>

<text>My experience with CKGS so far has been very positive. I applied for a passport renewal for myself and a tourist visa for my wife recently with successful outcomes in under 2 weeks for both cases.

The application process is definitely very convoluted with many documents to submit and having to go to the CKGS website first followed by the government website and then back to the CKGS website. However, once all the documents were submitted, the rest of the process was very smooth. There were automated notifications that kept us posted about how the application was proceeding. I got the passport back in less than 2 weeks (including weekends).

The visa application was submitted under a tight deadline as we were traveling in 2 weeks and our e-visa application had been rejected just then. I called CKGS through out the process to see if the application could be expedited and was able to connect with someone every time without any wait (other than navigating through the endless menu). Though they couldn't help me expedite the application, they were very patient and explained what and when to expect things to happen. I also dropped by the CKGS office in SF and the lady at the front desk was very helpful in answering my questions. When we were about 2 working days away from our travel, the lady understood our situation and said that she would take a note so her manager can send out an enquiry to the consulate. Luckily, we got the visa the same day before they had to send out the enquiry.

Overall, we had a very positive experience with CKGS and I would like to commend them for their professional service.</text>< Pictures>

<text>CKGS website is one of worst online portal for passport renewal application. To start with few things:

1. Language is super confusing on the website.
2. There is conflicting information at times and FAQs are not really helpful.
3. There is no Live Chat assistance provided for customers.
4. The so-called customer help service number charges the customer after first five minutes of the call. I am like "Are you serious??". Please don't call it Customer help service if you are charging customers for a valid enquiry or feedback call.

My husband applied for a passport renewal application online and attached all the supporting documents along with the original passport and the checklist as mentioned on the website. Once CKGS receives the application, it is natural that they are going to review it. Once they review it, if there is a missing document, they email you with the information (which is fair enough).
But the annoying part here is they email you the missing document one by one. That means, for example "document A" is missing, they are going to email you that Document A is missing and please return it within 7 days. Once you send the document to them via FedEx or UPS ( which causes a shipping fee of $15-$20 approximately from your pocket), they start reviewing again. Again they find something missing, they send you an email with a deadline of 7 days. So again you end up paying for UPS or FedEx shipment to send your document one by one. This gets too pricy.

Feedback:
1. It would be great if they could review the entire application and send the list of missing documents if any via email. The entire process can be made as ONE SINGLE STEP instead os series of back and forth.
2. The website can provide a Live chat assistance for customers
3. Please stop charging customers on the customer service call. That just doesn't sound fair.

My husband's passport renewal is still on hold with the status "Missing/Incomplete document" and I am still calling the customer service getting clarification on what is missing and being charged on my credit card for the number of minutes they put me on hold to get the correct information.

This service is ridiculous and I will not recommend this to anyone.</text>< Pics>

<text>Hi All,

I want to share my experience with CKGS and their office in San Francisco. I applied for my son's(minor) Indian Visa through them. I was little skeptical first and told my husband to just ditch the visa altogether and apply for E-Visa instead, as I was not comfortable with sending my son's passport. I read so many bad reviews and it just didn't feel good. It took a little while for me to understand to application procedure through CKGS website and Govt. of India website, but once I got the hang of it I was comfortable. After the initial glitch the next problem I had was shipping. They gave me the option of shipping through UPS/Fed ex from Me(Alaska) to them (CKGS SF), but when I tried to opt for the same from them to me back it didn't gave me any option. I thought of using shipping form them both ways as they charged $15, but may be because I am in Alaska it just didn't work. But after talking to the customer service they told me to use USPS prepaid label instead. Well I sent the application and after that it was a smooth process. They updated the status regularly. Sent us text and e-mail for the same. Finally we have our son's visa for 10 years to India. Thank you so much CKGS San Francisco for helping.

< review>
I actually had a great experience here, quite unlike most of the other reviewers. Everything went smoothly and I received my passport with an Indian tourist visa in it 8 business days after submitting the application (two days faster than they said it would take).

I followed the instructions on the Cox & Kings website exactly as they said and prepared all of the required documents. I booked an appointment online for 9am, showed up roughly 15 minutes before that, and went into this strange "pre-opening" room upstairs in an adjacent building that they have set up for people to wait before the actual office opens. This room had a LOT of people waiting in it, and I immediately though "oh crap... this is going to take all day." But then I showed my appointment confirmation to the attendant and got a ticket (people without appointments don't get these, so definitely make an appointment if you're submitting in person), then went downstairs to the actual office once it opened.

I waited there for about 15 minutes to see an attendant (the tickets are numbered and they call out the numbers one after another). It then took about 5 minutes with the attendant to submit my application and pay the fee. I was in and out within 40 minutes.

I received regular email notifications of the application process: receipt immediately after submission, notification of different steps of the process, and then a final notification with a tracking number when my passport was mailed out via Fedex.

I'm not sure why it went so badly for the other reviewers. Maybe it's only the people that have negative experiences that post here? Either way here's proof that it can actually go well at this place :)<//review>

I have good vision and I'm a lawyer, paperwork is my jam, and no, neither the form nor the CKGS instructions give any indication that I was required to sign the application.  Prepare yourself for extreme aggravation and extra expense.  Don't even get me going on how backward the application is with regard to a single, female parent of a minor applicant or the whole day the website didn't function and the link to the Indian government site was broken. I am left shaking my head in disbelief that more isn't being done to improve this service, but since CKGS has a state sanctioned monopoly, why bother, I guess.<//text>

I sent in my India tourist visa application and got my passport and visa back in a week.  Not the best but an acceptable experience.
1.	Confusing web page (hence the 3 starts).  The application forms are very complex. I have travelled 2/3 of the world and India‚Äôs application is the most complicated I have ever seen. They should just design one form for the people with Pakistan passport or Pakistan origin and give everybody else a break.
2.	Make sure your read and collect all the forms you need.  In my case, I need four forms.  Please not forget to attach a copy of your drive license to proof your address on the application is current.
3.	Since I lived in the Bay Area, I delivered the package myself.  Since CKGS will review your package, one will know if the application is completed or not on the site.  It is easier and quicker to correct the problem that way.
4.	The online appointment system was okay.  My wait at CKGS was about an hour (I watched the ‚ÄúIncredible India‚Äù commercial 8 times in the waiting room). When my number was called, a pleasant young lady reviewed my paper works and issued me a receipt within 5 minutes.
5.	Five business days later, the FedEx package showed up at my door step.  The saga was over.
6.	Most of the problem people have with the current system is that they did not fill the forms correctly or did not have all the necessary paper works.  One cannot blame CKGS on that front.<//Review>

<Text>In order to complete the visa application, my husband and I (with 3 postgraduate degrees between us) called their call center THREE times since things were so unclear on their website.

This was after submitting an OCI application for our son to the consulate directly, since there is NO indication on the consulate's website (after Googling OCI application) that one must use a 3rd party - by the time we figured that out, it was too late to apply for an OCI card. That is an issue with the consulate, but it still soured this experience.

After several hours of deciphering instructions (incidentally, middle names on passports go along with the first name in the "first name" field of the application), we finally completed all the forms, printed them, took them to the notary, thumbprinted our 17 month old (easier said than done), and brought them to the CKGS San Francisco center.

I was very frustrated with their website because (among other issues) once you select a mode of document delivery (drop off in person vs mail), you cannot change it. And for some reason, although I was initially allowed to make an appointment to drop off the documents, I had to cancel it because I realized I had to work on the day I had selected - then the website refused to allow me to make another appointment! We called the call center yet again about this; they said it was because we had selected "walk in" as our document delivery method...which makes no sense, as I had been able to make an initial appointment.

I mention this because once I arrived at the center, I had to wait in a line just to tell the greeting/desk person what I needed and get a number (she kept getting up and leaving when the people in front of me asked things), then it took nearly THREE hours to be called up, as I did not have an appointment. They tried to specifically call up people with appointments first, but many people just walked up once an agent was open, and were helped. This was quite frustrating.

Their overhead announcement system for calling numbers was broken, and anyone sitting in the 2nd waiting room could not hear numbers being called (I'm glad I got so hungry I had to use their vending machines shortly after arriving, or I might not have figured that part out). When I arrived, they were on non-appointment 610, and my number was 618 - it took over two hours to get through those 8 numbers because they called appointments and people kept going up out of turn.

Once it was finally my turn (around 2:45 PM, after arriving at noon), the experience was fairly pleasant; the agent was polite and helpful, and fortunately all of our documents were in order. We received our son's visa in the mail in less than a week - but we also mistakenly received someone else's passport!!!  His application number was listed to be the same as my son's (which it most definitely was not), so we got his passport. I have called them to find out what to do with the passport, and am awaiting a call back. I hope for his sake that he is not traveling in the next few weeks.

I would have given my overall experience two stars, since the agent was quite polite and helpful, and the visa came very quickly, even though there was a 3 hour wait - but getting someone else's passport in the mail was very frightening - that could just as easily have been my son's passport that was lost!

So, overall - if you can decipher the website, make sure to get your forms notarized/signed/thumbprinted (for kids under 5) appropriately, and have an appointment at the center, you could probably be in and out within an hour or two; otherwise, bring food and something to read, because you will be there for a LONG time. (FYI, their vending machines only take dollar bills).

And at the end of it all, you might not get your passport back, since they could send it to someone else!! If you are sure your documents are in order, it is much better to complete the entire transaction via mail.</Text>< Pics>

<text>This review is purely for the walk in application process.
I was suuuper nervous sending in my Visa Application via Cox and Kings. I went as a Walk In applicant initially -- which was a BIG mistake. The lines are really long, and a brief look at the Cox and Kings website will make it very clear that it is SUPER EASY to get an appointment for the next day.
**TIP (and I can't reiterate this enough)** : PLEASE MAKE AN APPOINTMENT - Making an appointment is very straightforward, it makes your life really really easy.
I took an appointment for the next day (got the first time slot - 9-10 am). There's a waiting room in the building if you arrive before 9 am, and my heart initially sank when I saw about 20 people waiting, and no sign of anyone from CKGS.
Just when I'd decided that it was going to be a really long wait - a CKGS representative showed up (they open at 9, he was in the room at 8:50), and in an Orderly fashion, started handing out Tokens - Emergencies/ OCI Matchups/ Visas.

I was Number 10 in the Visa line and I'd submitted my documentation/ gotten it verified by 9:30!

Couple of suggestions to make things better
- *It would be great to have an indicator on when the next available open slot for Visa appointment is in the landing page for the consulate*. After talking to people who'd showed up there, I realized it was mostly lack of information that was getting people to do WalkIns (the attitude was - ""I've heard there's no point getting an appointment anyways so I'm going to walk-in"". I had the same opinion, but realized how incorrect that was after seeing that I could easily get a next day appointment).
- It gets really ambiguous if there are a lot of people sitting in the Waiting room without any CKGS representative showing up. Please put up a sign saying *A CKGS representative will be here by 8:55 to hand out Tokens* - this would really help clear the confusion amongst people who show up early.

Tip for people coming in to submit their application via Walkin - please try to get the 9:00 am appointment. It'll be way quicker!< /text></record></dataset><record>

** Tips  **
- If your signatures on the applications do not match those on federally issued Ids (US passport) they WILL be returned, and you will then have 7 days to resubmit (no additional payment required). Most of us don't usually sign in perfect style everytime, or even daily, so this can cause some lost time.
- If the applicant is a minor and a US citizen, always submit the parents Naturalization certificate, even if that is not spelled out clearly in the checklist.<//review>
